< Text>
This place is a well oiled machine!  Once you walk in (only one way in), a very nice employee hands you a  sample of ham then guides you around the corner to the ordering line. Once it's your turn, all you have to do is let the cashier know what you want. Everything is labeled on the refrigerator doors behind them. After they box/wrap everything up for you, they will even help you to your vehicle.  All the food is excellent and just the right amount.  We'll definitely order again.<//Text>

<text>It's got the air of a hole in the wall restaurant from the outside, but do not judge them by the exterior. it really does have the best Mediterranean food in the area. They have a vegetarian plate which is really just the sides grouped together as a single plate, so my vegetarian friends weren't overly impressed, but I love the lule, the kabobs, and the sides are super flavorful even if not filling by themselves. The salmon also got high marks from my friend. The prices are reasonable too.

It's in an industrial area where there aren't many comparable options nearby and the locals like this place so be prepared. If you get there at noon, you should get a table without too much trouble. Get there at 12:30 though and you might have to wait.< /text>< pictures>

A friend and I tried this little out-of-the way restaurant for dinner, mext to a marine repair shop. An add place for a restaurant, I thought. It was deserted the evening we went... not another customer in sight. Too bad, because the food was very good. While service was a little slow, the grape leaves, and chicken kabobs were delicious and the portions were generous. We also loved the eggplant caviar-- it was fresh-tasting and served cold, but with the great pita bread, it was very satisfying and a perfect start to the meal. The only downside comment I have is that the Greek salad was pretty standard and nothing special.</text>

I cannot say enough good things about this quaint little hole in the wall.  The food is outstanding!!!  I eat here on a weekly basis.  It is a hidden gem.  Everything I have tried is fantastic.  I usually get the greek chicken salad or the chicken breast kabob plate.
The fries are really scrumptious.  Surprising that they have fries, but they are truly really good.

I love that I can call ahead and place my order and it is ready within minutes of my arrival.  They do tons of delivery and take out.
Drive by slow to find the place, it's an unassuming storefront.  I highly recommend if you like Mediterranean.</review>

<user_id>109337514451247023352< /user_id><user_name>Ron Quan</user_name>< date>
1461985882828</date>
< Rating>
4< /Rating>
< Text>
Oddly situated restaurant in the middle of an industrial area in Burbank. You'd easily drive by this place without a second thought. The interior is relatively spare but seats more than you'd expect.

I ordered to go and the beef in the beef salad was still tender and juicy even after sitting in the to-go box for an hour. The ikra was one of the better ones I've had. I'm not sure why it's universally called eggplant caviar because there's no caviar nor eggs for that matter. The Armenian coffee was strong without a huge amount of sludge.

Parking is plentiful on the other side of the street with diagonal stalls set along the entire street.<//Text>

<Time>1393835925267< /Time><Rate>5<//Rate>< Text>
Great spot! It's my new go-to before or after a flight out of Burbank--the airport is literally a 3 minute drive.

The food is fantastic. A heaping plate of two pieces of flavorful lule kebab on rice plus two samplings of their appetizers (love the smoky eggplant dip and tzatziki-like yogurt dip) and pita will set you back $6.75. A sprinkling of sumac seals the deal.

The place is a local, family-owned restaurant with friendly and attentive waitstaff. They have beers on tap and apparently live music on Saturdays to keep things festive. Looking forward to returning again and again.< /Text>

<pics>None< /pics><Text>I was unlucky enough to have a deer damage my vehicle during evacuation with my family from the recent Santa Cruz wildfires.

As we have bundled home and auto insurance with State Farm I elected to get my vehicle repaired and  only wanted the best bodyshop to do the work. Once the shop inspected the damage I lodged a claim easily using the StateFarm phone app in around 10 minutes.

<review>Greetings friends of San Jose! My name is Michael, and I recently moved to California from the East Coast. Though my only experience for insurance has been with State Farm, my time with Aaron has certainly been my best (from 3 states over ten years).

Moving from any state comes with many challenges. One of those challenges is a long list of transfers, such as car insurance, dental, school, etc. My agent 2100 miles away knew of Aaron and recommended him wholeheartedly. Still, I felt inclined to do my due diligence and researched several agents in Silicon Valley to ensure I would be taken care of if an emergency arose, God forbid. Don't waste your time researching-- this office is good people and deserve your resources. Bridgette handled my move seamlessly and made me feel a part of the San Jose community before I even got off the plane. Not only did she communicate with the Atlanta office without me lifting a finger, but she recommended places to live, restaurants to eat, and sites to experience.

Upon my arrival, a meeting at the office (on a Saturday, nonetheless) was recommended, but I could not find the time to get into the office. I called Aaron on the phone, introduced myself, and had a small conversation. Most of you will agree that seldom do actual agents take the time to speak with you, especially about smaller ticket items or just to check in. Aaron is available at any time if you feel that you need to speak with the 'big boss'. He will be there for your family, and he will make sure you are taken care of. Even on Saturdays...

The service Aaron's team has provided me to date has been nothing but spectacular. I would recommend any insurance customer (Auto, Home, etc.) in the Bay Area to consider this team to take care of you... In times of need, Aaron, Bridgette, Sean, and the rest of the crew in Campbell will make sure you feel important, and help you survive some of the most difficult times in life. I wholeheartedly suggest you give Aaron a chance. It will be a 5-star experience.

Best,

< Review>
Biddle park is great if youre looking for alone time or to avoid regular park crowds. There's hardly anyone there at any given time, except for the few who take their dogs to run off leash. (Leash law is loosely enforced.) The park itself isn't maintained except for the soccer field which is nicely mowed. Just watch out for the random drug deals that are known to take place in the back corner of the park.</Review>

<gmap_id>0x8094661ae2f29897:0x5c03757451ab60bd</gmap_id><user>100931992862066718825</user><Name>Sir G.</Name>< Review>
Just an FYI to all public and towing companies. If you as a registered owner can prove that your car was disabled at the time that it was towed, then you should be able to get refunded for the towing cost because by law, disabled cars (inoperable or broken) need to get a 24 hour notice that it will be towed if not moved, per the CVC. I do agree that tow truck operators take great safety risks while performing their duties, however when it comes to predatory towing I loose all respect for them. At the same time, such illegal practices keep people in check but at a high cost to the registered owners. I mean $330 for a few minutes of storage is excessive, reminds me of "cruel and unusual punishment" in a monetary sense. I witnessed this company in question take my friends car very, very quietly in less than 30 seconds. I was amazed and late to confront the operator.  We followed it all the way to the tow yard, the driver said we would have to pick it up at the yard and not on the spot even though my buddy was willing to pay for the fees on the spot (road). Another point to keep in mind public, if you catch the operator still inside any apartment complex with your car being towed you have the right to demand the return of your car on the spot and without producing an ID or a DL per California law. The tow truck operator has to return your car immediately or you can sue them for 4 times greater than what the fees would be.< /Review>
< Date>
1477492658140</Date>
<Resp>{'time': 1477415730337, 'text': 'Well, let us correct that misinformation.\n\nIf you are parked on someone\'s private property you are subject to the owners rules at all times.\n\nIf you are in a fire lane, handicap stall, reserved parking stall, blocking a driveway or in some other type of "No Parking" area you may be subject to immediate tow - there is no "24 hour disabled vehicle waiver".\n\nThat type of warning is reserved for a vehicle that is missing an engine or other legally required equipment necessary to operate on a highway.\n\nOtherwise, if the vehicle looks disabled or abandoned (such as expired tags, flat tires, very dirty, etc) the property management may post a 96 hour warning on the vehicle and have it removed if it is still on the property when the warning expires.\n\nPlease understand there is a difference between what a law enforcement officer is required to do prior to towing a vehicle on public property / highway access and a property management company removing vehicles from private property - there is a huge difference.'}</Resp></record>

<Rate>2</Rate>< Text>
The 16% service charge, 3% healthy LA fee, 10% sales tax all BEFORE A TIP, is 35-40% extra.

Keep in mind the statement says, ‚ÄòEntirety of the charge will be retained by the company‚Äô. So, I guess we still have to tip if we want to help the servers and the company keeps our fees?

A normal business model would have operating cost built into the price of food.

I understand a restaurant charging extra for a 6 course meal, but hard to justify when it‚Äôs a fast table delivery with plastic silverware.

Still arguably the best chicken schnitzel in town, but hard to justify paying $46 for a water and chicken bowl over lunch.< /Text>

< Text>
Overall fast service even with long lines. Seating can be challenging if you're coming in a larger party.
Minimal parking in the area.
We got the porridge with mushrooms, good flavors overall with crunch from corn and good mushroom flavors. There was supposed to be a poached egg but by the time I received it had hardened.
Got the tartar and thought it was underwhelming. Not bad but not something I'd get again, didn't enjoy the cream and tartar. Maybe if it had more pepper or stronger microgreens.
Definitely a hipster feel to it with decent pricing. Good for families and small groups. Good portion sizes as well which is why I gave it 4 stars, flavors were just not there for me.
Chocolate mousse dessert was good, creamy and in between a pudding and mousse texture with good balance of nuts at the base.

I have yet to find only a handful really good breakfast/brunch spots in LA unfortunately this is not one of them.< /Text>

<Text>Finally had a chance to check out this daytime-only spot which had long been on my bucket list. I hope that I could have their oatmeal as my breakfast every day. Their beef tartare was very delicious as well - the seasoning did not steal the scene but brought out the original and rich flavor of the beef. I was also impressed by the innovative roasted cone cabbage - it was tender and tasted wonderful. For dessert, it was a genius idea to combine chocolate mousse and cucumber sherbet.

It was fun to notice some recurring ingredients in their food, such as skyr ("technically classified as cheese, although widely regarded as yogurt"), almond butter, and a green powder that had a strong sour taste. What a pity that I could not try everything on their menu at one time. Look forward to visiting this place again.

Update: This time we ventured into the more uncharted territory of taste. The roasted carrots and blood oranges (dyed purple) had a refreshing taste of beer and I loved the ricotta at the bottom. As for the spelt porridge, I personally found the creamy porridge itself more agreeable than the bitter roast flavor at the top. Overall, I would not use a label of "weird" to dismiss the unexpected experience, and on the contrary I appreciate all the innovation and daringness embodied in these plates.

P.S. The pics sort of show how the dishes were initially arranged and what they looked like inside.
.
.
.

<pictures>None<//pictures><user>100163385729683234643< /user><user_name>Jesse Caster</user_name>< Review>
The name of this restaurant conjures dramatic imagery to forefront of one's mind. Yet to my delight I walk through the front door and up to the pristine yet modest counter. The immediate vibe equal parts serene dojo meets reverent art gallery. So having followed the rise of Chef Jordan Kahn with keen interest I have waited to enjoy this eating experience, timing my future meal so I could selfishly soak it up completely on my own without interruption. I was not disappointed in the slightest. The line cooks and chefs are dressed reminiscent of the staff at the Masonic Marciano Art Foundation.

The kitchen takes up the majority of the space where you order with the menu projected on the wall to your right as you face the counter. Every piece of decor toward the window had the afternoon sun gently illuminating it stocked with deliberately spaced items in mason jars and vials, with their house made lattes, teas and kombuchas in the corresponding refrigerated display case that looked like it was on loan from Andy Warhol's Studio.

The serenity of space suddenly sprang into a harmonious orchestrated ballet once I placed my order; all to curious as to what would be their take on a Crispy Chicken Schnitzel. Truth be told, I was set to compare it to the one I have had at Spago Beverly Hills, as it is the recipe of Chef Wolfgang's Grandmother. It was an Absolute Night and Day contrast. The high end comfort food with generous portions harkins back to Wolf's Grandmother's dinner table, a true delicious classic. However, in line with everything Jordan Kahn has created thus far in his career his recipes and presentation are; what if the Tesla decided to reimagine food in a galaxy far far away. Mouth watering crispy chicken coated in salsa seca topped with herbaceous shaved black kale and bright preserved lemon. Immaculately presented center of plate with absolutely nothing out of place.</Review>

< Text>
Went in to buy a black coffee and a very overpriced jar of pistachio almond butter $14 (6/8oz.) I'm sure they put way more almond in it and charge much more for the pistachio addition...

For the coffee to go and the almond butter off the shelf, the employee tacked on their 16% PLUS 3%  "Surcharge"....that's before 10% sales tax and any tip they almost compel you to leave! That's getting to 35-40% tax+tip on your meal.

Charge what you want for your food + drink but enough with these sneaky surcharges. The employee could EASILY have not hit me with the nearly 20% surcharge considering it was a quick coffee and an item on the shelf. Unfortunately he did not and I had to ask to remove the extra $5 which he did. They are banking on you feeling too ashamed to ask for the surcharge removal.

This is a minimalistic, pretentious, yet somewhat creative and incredibly overpriced small portioned (you'll leave hungry) restaurant run by people who think they are they second coming of Noma. I will not be returning. The coffee was quite poor as well.</Text>

Jasmin Hussain</name>
<Date>1539801699075< /Date><rating>5</rating>< Text>
This restaurant is easily missed driving by in the seemingly industrial but trendy area of Culver City. Though word of mouth spread quickly about this hidden lunch spot, making it quite busy during the lunch hours 12pm ‚Äì 2pm. Crowd quickly dissolves after 2pm, great time to come if you want to have a quiet lunch; or otherwise, come during breakfast when it is generally not that crowded. The Chicken confit which comes with heirloom grits, spigarello, and roasted strawberry tastes comforting with the strong chicken taste along with some nice twists from the spigarello and roasted toppings. I could not taste the strawberry that much, but tasted some roasted garlic which I assume was roasted together with the strawberry. The Namelaka is a chocolate cream on top of toasted almonds topped with I assume were cucumber iced shavings. Coffees are great and have a rich taste. The menu is en par with modern technological progress projected on a wall via multi-media. The restaurant looks neat and clean, and according to the minimalist style, only furnished with a few tables. There is more space in front of the restaurant to sit and on the adjacent patio. Parking is hit and miss and depends on the timing I guess. Overall, this restaurant is great to experience fresh and different food during your lunch time as a nice escape from office. The restaurant is only open Monday ‚Äì Fridays from 8am ‚Äì 5pm.

Update:

Raw almond oatmeal

Sounds simple but get your taste buds ready for a oatmeal filled of flavors underlined by a smooth note.

Icelandic rye bread with butter and preserves is served with a big chunk of rye bread making the dish pretty filling. Be ready to exercise your palate. Containing lots of grains and seeds requiring patience to chew. The rich, dark flavor of the bread demands something to contrast with which could possibly be something sweetish. However the preserves don't do the job being very sour.< /Text>

< Review>
A breakfast and a lunch at Destroyer.
---
Breakfast.

Drinks: White tea & espresso

1: raw oatmeal, almond milk, red currant, vanilla

(Really F'n tasty. Multilayered. Best oatmeal I've ever had. I know it's "just oatmeal"... but it's not.)

2: icelandic rye bread, cultured butter, preserves

(The bread was very good and is so dense, it's a meal by itself. Not crazy about the butter or preserves since the flavor of the bread overpowered it. Salted Kerrygold would have been better and easier.)

3: organic hen egg, crispy potato, mushroom

(Oh man! This was really great. A real surprise. I literally have to dig into it. It's a treasure.)
---
Lunch at Destroyer...

- beef tartare, smoked egg cream, pickled mushroom, chicory

(This was really good. The sour bitter taste of the chicory was very nice with the smooth and cool beef mixture. It benefits by taking heaping bites!)

- roasted baby yams, avocado, yogurt, walnut

(This was subtle and fine. Pretty to look at and fun to eat. Nothing "spectacular", but it's a nice cool treat. I like the procedural process of eating it. Making "full taste" bites with every ingredient on your fork. Fulfilling.)

- bavarian cream, toffee, apple, sorrel

(Cream with apple sauce and sweet crunchy toffee. It's not much without the sorrel. So careful big bites help here. You have to build your bites because it becomes a big mess if you're not careful. Yummy desert. But it's nothing if any piece is missing.)< /Review>

<text>Destroyer was an extremely pleasant surprise for me. I thought it was going to be one of those cool hip innovative artisan restaurants with tiny portion sizes for an absurd price that I would go for the experience but leave still hungry and wanting more but the portion sizes were actually quite large!!

I think what really makes Destroyer stand out is the outstanding food presentation and the flavor combinations that are truly one of a kind. I mean never have I had rice porridge with puffed rice and burnt onions before, or mushrooms combined with arugula, spelt, and cheese before. The mushrooms and cauliflower were def my favorite of what I got and even with splitting this with a friend we still had plenty leftover that we were able to eat the next day!

I would absolutely recommend trying Destroyer at least once for the experience. The plating and presentation are gorgeous and the unique blend of foods should be more than enough to pique your interest. You can tell that each dish is thoughtfully created and presented and you can even see them in the kitchen carefully placing everything in the dish. I know the taste probably won't appeal to everyone but it still is an incredibly aesthetic and different dining experience.</text><Time>1582025448221</Time>< Rate>
5</Rate>

Heather Allen< /username>
<Time>1586981640723< /Time><Rate>5<//Rate>< review>
I write for a music and coffee blog called Crooners In Coffeeshops, in which I interview local musicians at local coffeeshops. My writeup reflects the positive experience that I encountered at Destroyer on our interview date.

Word of mouth has spread through the Westside (as well as many a Los Angeles based food blog) about a cafe that serves delicious high-end bites for a relatively affordable price, and that cafe Destroyer. The chic, modern minimalist shop strives to bring fresh, organic, and homemade recipes to any guest that steps through its doors. Apart from the intriguing blend of sweet, smokey, and savory scents that graze your nose, your eyes will naturally shoot to its environmentally friendly projected menu, and boy, are you in for a treat.

Destroyer‚Äôs offerings include basic coffee options (espresso based drinks primarily), teas, and tonics amongst an impressive menu split into grains (oatmeals and breads), cold (veggie and light protein), hot (heavier proteins with healthy starches), and sweet (exactly what you would imagine to be gourmet dessert). I chose to go for a latte and the Spiced Apricot Bread, which was a glorious blend of fresh fruit, creme fraiche, and red currant. Believe me when I say that these meals are meant to be slowly savored, and if you‚Äôre lucky to nab yourself a seat in one of their coveted indoor tables, shaded patio area or benched bistro tables, jump on it and enjoy the journey that your tastebuds are about to experience.<//review>

< text>
Destroyer is a solid breakfast/lunch spot in Los Angeles/Culver City. It's in an interesting part of town and the building itself is minimalism design forward. The menu is cleanly projected onto the white wall near the register.

My buddy and I ordered the avocado toast with burnt onion and a porridge with mushrooms. Both were unique and come out on beautifully simple plates. However, both dishes could have been salted more.

Overall, Destroyer was a good experience with a more healthy menu in a beautiful space.< /text>

1571327748160</Date>
<rating>4</rating>< Text>
This is more of an experience than a meal, but I like it!! Very light and healthy. There is an earthy note to all the dishes.

Sweet potato is a must (they keep the skin on because the skin is full of nutrients! You won't be able to taste much difference so just try it!) tip: eat the bitter endives with the sweet potato and then a bite of avocado for added creaminess!

Beet salad is good, plenty of quinoa and the burst of black berries in between the bitterness of the grain was incredibly pleasant, paired with the sweet beets contrasted by the horseradish powder sprinkled on top.

Spelt porridge was a bit too earthy for me, as in one mellow shroomy note! It was still good..I'd add a bit of ginger or sesame oil to add another contrastive element to it! Therefore, have it with a side of something acidic.

Then there are the dessert, which I heard was incredible by the table sitting next to us. This was my 2nd food stop so was too full to try. Can't wait to check it out again next time.

Tip: this place is located in a really cool area, great for taking Instagram photos so plan accordingly</Text>

<user_id>117411460679532736731</user_id>< text>
Seems pricy, at around $30 for lunch + coffee + tip, but its the same chef as Vespertine across the street, so its surprisingly affordable for a Micheline Star luxury experience!

Always superb service, fast for what it is, and take-out is available (although the presentation is where its at, so I highly recommend dining in).

Limited seating, impossible to find street parking (you'll get towed ASAP for parking in the office lots around the area), so expect to park a bit far and walk.

Great place to bring out-of-town friends, as this feels "very LA".

Judging from the outfits the other patrons wear, this seems to be an Instagram hotspot, if this is an interest.

Casual or formal, no dresscode or judgement from the friendly staff.</text>

Destroyer is a strange and wonderful gift I stumbled upon. The space is small but there‚Äôs seating outdoors, and it‚Äôs neat to see the open kitchen, watching them delicately and lovingly create each dish. Everyone that works there is very kind and helpful. The food is phenomenal and beautifully crafted. I had the chicken confit, and I couldn‚Äôt have been more pleased. My coworkers had the roasted  cone cabbage and steak tartare. Just so you know, you order at the front and they give you a number and bring it to you when it‚Äôs ready. The food comes out very quickly. There is staff walking about to get anything else you might need. If you order dessert you just let one of them know when you‚Äôre ready for it to be prepared.<//review>

<Time>1475181545907<//Time>< Review>
I think you need to try this.

It's only been open about 2.5 weeks as of this writing so they still have some kinks to work out in the service area but the food was really impressive.

Food - we split the beets (cold) and the yam (hot)  I hate quinoa.  I now love quinoa!  Toasted and fried sprinkled on some lovely beets with avocado.  WOW i was shocked and impressed with how this tasted.

The yam with caramelized onions was good but unfortunately far too salty for me.  It was still full of amazing flavor and I'm just having an issue with salt these days personally.  Lately when I think something is far too salty other people I'm with think it's fine.  So, I'm not sure I can ding Destroyer for this.

They have a breakfast menu live on their website and start serving lunch at 11.30

They are not yet currently open on weekends but hope to in another month or so.< /Review>
